    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143239038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3686206965062384599">An incredible read. An ironically heartwarming and comforting message is prominent within this unique picture book. The illustrations are exceptionally memorable and suit the style of the book perfectly- it provides a beautiful opportunity to discuss the topic of death with children without it being daunting or frightening but rather more gentle and comforting. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_523581505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523581505" />
    <a title="Catherine Nichols" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5943070-catherine-nichols"><img alt="Catherine Nichols" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442456124p2/5943070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/523581505?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine Nichols" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine Nichols" href="/user/show/5943070-catherine-nichols">Catherine Nichols</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer523581505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13311595992410708644">This is not your usual picture book about death. The story is simple. Death, wearing a fashionably long plaid coat and bearing a black tulip, comes to stay with Duck. Understandably nervous, Duck asks, "Are you going to make something happen?" But no. "Life takes care of that," Death tells her. The two pal around, going to the pond, perching high in a tree. Duck wonders about dying and Death listens to her speculate. Winter comes, and one night Duck lies down. She does not get up. Death gently p</span>
  <span id="freeText13311595992410708644" style="display:none">This is not your usual picture book about death. The story is simple. Death, wearing a fashionably long plaid coat and bearing a black tulip, comes to stay with Duck. Understandably nervous, Duck asks, "Are you going to make something happen?" But no. "Life takes care of that," Death tells her. The two pal around, going to the pond, perching high in a tree. Duck wonders about dying and Death listens to her speculate. Winter comes, and one night Duck lies down. She does not get up. Death gently places her body in the river, the tulip resting on her chest.<br /><br />Written and illustrated by Wolf Erlbruch, a German author, (and beautifully translated by Catherine Chidgey), the book's simple text and sparse, elegant illustrations combine to create a moving yet unsentimental treatise on death. It also has a sly, deadpan humor throughout, as when Duck first notices Death's presence. "Duck was scared stiff, and who could blame her?"<br /><br />A strange (in the best sense), moving book, it isn't for every child. But I wish it had been around when I was one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13311595992410708644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2142759258" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2142759258" />
    <a title="Niamh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52346651-niamh"><img alt="Niamh" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2142759258?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niamh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niamh" href="/user/show/52346651-niamh">Niamh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52346651-niamh?shelf=picturebooks">picturebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2142759258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15123891886105215396">‘Duck, Death and the Tulip’ written and illustrated by German author Wolf Erlbruch synthesises the presentation of human, animal and nature forms and sensitively presents death through metaphorical pictures as the eponymous title suggests. The picture book offers all types of readers the opportunity to learn about death in a unique and accessible way whilst presenting death in the form of a character carrying a black tulip which begins to naturally die along with the Duck, as the story progresse</span>
  <span id="freeText15123891886105215396" style="display:none">‘Duck, Death and the Tulip’ written and illustrated by German author Wolf Erlbruch synthesises the presentation of human, animal and nature forms and sensitively presents death through metaphorical pictures as the eponymous title suggests. The picture book offers all types of readers the opportunity to learn about death in a unique and accessible way whilst presenting death in the form of a character carrying a black tulip which begins to naturally die along with the Duck, as the story progresses. Throughout the story, the pictures and words effectively work together through the words and pictures complimenting each other. For example, the book opens with the narrator describing how for a while, ‘Duck had had a feeling’ and noticed something always creeping behind with the simplistic illustration of the duck curiously peering behind. On the opposite page, stands death as a figure (which our eyes our instantly drawn to) which simply answers the duck’s enquiry as to who they are as, ‘I am death’. By presenting these two characters as opposing each other from the start, this awakens curiosity in the reader to find out why Death is following Duck whilst perhaps hinting to older readers that Duck is dying. In the book, Erlbuch’s use of language alongside the simplistic pictures effectively depicts duck and death sharing conversations about duck’s impending death and death answering questions about Duck’s ideas on the afterlife whilst having fun together. <br /><br />Personally, I think if I were sharing this with children I would choose to read this in smaller shared or guided reading groups due to the various chances for ‘zooming in’ with children and exploring certain parts such as, Duck’s ideas on the afterlife or the poignancy of the final page. Additionally, I think the amount of opportunities for rich discussion this book provides children should be given time and attention, particularly if children have not experienced or understand what grief is. <br /><br />I couldn't recommend this book more-it takes a difficult subject and effectively provides a beautifully comforting story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15123891886105215396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5014330675029465097">I don't know what I was expecting, I didn't read the blurb but requested it at work after a colleague told me about it. Is this literary fiction for children?! Death is a dark subject of course, but I'm not sure I'd read this to my 5 year old. It's a great concept. Just not for me. It's not harmful, but quite confronting, as are the illustrations. This would be excellent for the right time, a good resource for the subject of death.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92743421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7586291977928384641">Now translated into English, Death, Duck and Tulip.<br/>Well after I found my way into the 'issues' section at the library searching for childrens laureate Anthony Browne I came across this book.Id heard the title recently after a librarian friend told me how they had ordered several of them to help children deal with death, but after reading them they had doubts they would be appropriate for children. The blurb says adults and teenagers and I think that if intended for younger age groups extreme cau</span>
  <span id="freeText7586291977928384641" style="display:none">Now translated into English, Death, Duck and Tulip.<br />Well after I found my way into the 'issues' section at the library searching for childrens laureate Anthony Browne I came across this book.Id heard the title recently after a librarian friend told me how they had ordered several of them to help children deal with death, but after reading them they had doubts they would be appropriate for children. The blurb says adults and teenagers and I think that if intended for younger age groups extreme caution must be used. Death is with the duck from page 1, shown as a skeleton face thing but clothed in beige colours ( not your black grim reaper ). The duck asks lots of quetions and is not afraid and welcomes deaths presence, even warming death with his own body when death becomes cold and wet in the pond. If your in the unfortunate position of having to explain to a child about death, maybe a family member is dying then this book hopefully would take the fear of death away. But as I read it under normal circumstances it really does give you the creeps and I would not recommend for very young children. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7586291977928384641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13803856370372819071" style="display:none">25/52 books read in 2019.<br /><br />I just had to re-read because it is so precious &amp; I still haven't brought it back to the library. <br />My review still stands.<br /><br />20/52 books read in 2019.<br /><br />EN: I absolutely adore this picture book. It is short, sweet, and the illustrations are beautiful. I think it would be the perfect way to explain a sudden passing or death in general to children. The entire book feels incredibly peaceful and I think that is incredibly important when you inform a child about this natural process so you do not add unnecessary fear.<br />I definitely want to read it again!<br /><br />NL: Dit is zeker weten een van mijn favoriete prentenboeken. Het is kort, lief en de illustraties zijn prachtig. Ik denk dat dit boek enorm handig kan zijn als je aan een kind moet uitleggen dat iemand overleden is, of ze vragen hebben over de dood. Het boek voelt enorm vredig en dat lijkt mij de perfecte manier om dit natuurlijke proces uit te leggen zonder onnodige angst in te boezemen.<br />Ik wil dit verhaal zeker nog een keertje lezen!</span>

    <a title="Harriet Mitchell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9299398-harriet-mitchell"><img alt="Harriet Mitchell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564522321p2/9299398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1450766125?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harriet Mitchell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harriet Mitchell" href="/user/show/9299398-harriet-mitchell">Harriet Mitchell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781877467141" href="/book/show/4009037-duck-death-and-the-tulip">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1450766125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17578120669384255788">This book is an excellent conversation starter. It covers the topic of death in a simple and effective way. It provides the reader(s) a safe space to discuss the difficult subject matter.<br/><br/>Simply taking just a picture or double page spread could be a way to initiate discussion with others. It could link to RE and different views of life after death.<br/><br/>Considering how simple the text and images are, there is an incredible amount you can take from them. The use of blank space and of colour are also use</span>
  <span id="freeText17578120669384255788" style="display:none">This book is an excellent conversation starter. It covers the topic of death in a simple and effective way. It provides the reader(s) a safe space to discuss the difficult subject matter.<br /><br />Simply taking just a picture or double page spread could be a way to initiate discussion with others. It could link to RE and different views of life after death.<br /><br />Considering how simple the text and images are, there is an incredible amount you can take from them. The use of blank space and of colour are also used highly effectively and the significance of this could even be talked about in an art lesson.<br /><br />It would be helpful for the implied reader to have an awareness of life and death, some knowledge of predators and prey and an awareness of potential danger. <br /><br />The symbolism behind tulips/ flowers is an interesting further discussion point.<br /><br />Readers will have their own preconceptions on the topic but these may be challenged as a result of the discussion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17578120669384255788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2211844249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2211844249" />
    <a title="Ellie Labbett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73493292-ellie-labbett"><img alt="Ellie Labbett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568719069p2/73493292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2211844249?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellie Labbett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellie Labbett" href="/user/show/73493292-ellie-labbett">Ellie Labbett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73493292-ellie-labbett?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73493292-ellie-labbett?shelf=nature">nature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73493292-ellie-labbett?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73493292-ellie-labbett?shelf=bereavement">bereavement</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2211844249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8956456304733189594"> Erlbruch opens a window into aging and the cycle of life and death in this stunning picture book, which extends into an unlikely friendship between two characters named Duck and Death. There is something so touching about the warmth to which Duck welcomes Death, despite the associations and fears surrounding the character. Perhaps even more affecting is the flicker of mourning that Death feels for Duck after his passing, regardless of being possibly desensitized by such a process. <br/> The gentlene</span>
  <span id="freeText8956456304733189594" style="display:none"> Erlbruch opens a window into aging and the cycle of life and death in this stunning picture book, which extends into an unlikely friendship between two characters named Duck and Death. There is something so touching about the warmth to which Duck welcomes Death, despite the associations and fears surrounding the character. Perhaps even more affecting is the flicker of mourning that Death feels for Duck after his passing, regardless of being possibly desensitized by such a process. <br /> The gentleness to which death is shown to be an inevitable part of life is genuinely beautiful, but I felt like this was more than just a tale to lessen fears about those that may depart from our lives. It unflinchingly accepts death at all levels, making no promises about what becomes of you after passing away. What might be seen as a coldness and may be uncomforting for some, I see as necessary for those who feel that their hearts hold no alternative answer. An afterlife is something that even Duck ponders about, which will of course be mirrored in many readers, making the character more distinctly human than ever. However, Death offers no shield to protect Duck from the process of dying itself, which is resoundingly just a part of life. I think that this offers a resolute answer that will genuinely help some readers to move forwards.<br />I am increasingly intrigued by the delicacy of Erlbruch’s use of symbolism, and evermore so by his illustrations, holding a minimality that is so intrinsic to the themes within the story. I do not think that there is an emptiness in this. So much is said by using so little, again, perhaps linking back to the focus upon reality and absence of other explanations. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8956456304733189594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2379566788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5934734255586994518">This is easily one of the most moving books I’ve ever read. The portrayal of how one can make friends with death and is not something to fear has truly stuck with me. Such a powerful message and I can’t recommend this book highly enough!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2076114737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12705743566037089594">I originally read this picture book (which was originally published in German in 2007) back in April, when I was visiting a dear friend in New Zealand. I was in the middle of a break-up and was feeling pretty overwhelmingly sad, and she had this book checked out from the library and left it outside the door of the room I was staying in for me to read. I read it, and liked it, enough that I kept thinking about it and eventually checked it out from the library back home in Brooklyn. <br/><br/>The art is rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12705743566037089594" style="display:none">I originally read this picture book (which was originally published in German in 2007) back in April, when I was visiting a dear friend in New Zealand. I was in the middle of a break-up and was feeling pretty overwhelmingly sad, and she had this book checked out from the library and left it outside the door of the room I was staying in for me to read. I read it, and liked it, enough that I kept thinking about it and eventually checked it out from the library back home in Brooklyn. <br /><br />The art is really lovely, with cut-out style pencil drawings of our protagonists (Duck and Death) and other collage elements, too. The text is straightforward but graceful and sometimes funny, in a way that works with the story, in which Duck learns of the presence of Death in her life/in life in general, and becomes comfortable with him, despite how fearful she is at first. The whole thing is excellent.<br /><br />You can see a whole bunch of art from this book on <a href="https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/05/04/duck-death-and-the-tulip-wolf-erlbruch/" rel="nofollow noopener">Brain Pickings</a>, though scrolling through the images on a screen isn't quite as satisfying (for me, anyway) as turning pages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12705743566037089594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3614818005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3614818005" />
    <a title="Macey Giberson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120080124-macey-giberson"><img alt="Macey Giberson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597763524p2/120080124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3614818005?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Macey Giberson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Macey Giberson" href="/user/show/120080124-macey-giberson">Macey Giberson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120080124-macey-giberson?shelf=animals-other-protagonist">animals-other-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120080124-macey-giberson?shelf=artistic">artistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120080124-macey-giberson?shelf=appreciation">appreciation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120080124-macey-giberson?shelf=valuable-lesson">valuable-lesson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120080124-macey-giberson?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120080124-macey-giberson?shelf=grief">grief</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3614818005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11392765375270941234">This story was well portrayed in a way that is friendly for children to read and comprehend. In this story, the way the narrator illustrates death is through a child-like body, but the image of a skeleton to replace it. By doing this, the author and illustrating present death to be seen as a human and make sure that the children realize that everyone and everything will eventually experience death. However, it is not something to be scared of this is because it is only there to support you as yo</span>
  <span id="freeText11392765375270941234" style="display:none">This story was well portrayed in a way that is friendly for children to read and comprehend. In this story, the way the narrator illustrates death is through a child-like body, but the image of a skeleton to replace it. By doing this, the author and illustrating present death to be seen as a human and make sure that the children realize that everyone and everything will eventually experience death. However, it is not something to be scared of this is because it is only there to support you as you proceed onto the next phase in the afterlife. By having death place a tulip onto duck after she passed away, there is this sense of sympathy and love that is attached to death from the audience's perspective. That death wants duck's body to rest in peace. The foreshadowing of death placing duck in water was made when duck states that she will miss the pond once she is dead. That brings the story full circle and demonstrates this moral lesson that things happen for a reason and that you can't be scared of that reason. You just have to accept it, make amends with it, and continue living your life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11392765375270941234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251874286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1134605742652328507">We're not entirely sure how to feel about this particular book, it follows the story of a duck who one day realises that death is following her and they form a somewhat simplistic friendship where Duck speculates about what happens after death and Death allows her to without offering any specifics. <br/><br/>We can say that is does cover the subject of death very effectively despite the simple way in which the story is conveyed. Would probably leave this story until children are old enough to have an awar</span>
  <span id="freeText1134605742652328507" style="display:none">We're not entirely sure how to feel about this particular book, it follows the story of a duck who one day realises that death is following her and they form a somewhat simplistic friendship where Duck speculates about what happens after death and Death allows her to without offering any specifics. <br /><br />We can say that is does cover the subject of death very effectively despite the simple way in which the story is conveyed. Would probably leave this story until children are old enough to have an awareness of death though, there is something quite chilling about the illustrations of Death in our opinion!<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2144664882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2144664882" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70883817-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507233390p2/70883817.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2144664882?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/70883817-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2144664882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3944763613761032967">I wasn't sure what to make of this book. I think it makes a bold attempt at dealing with death, in a way that presents children with the truth. The characterof death is not to be feared, but simply a part of life.<br/><br/>Its very 'to the point', so it is definitely one to think carefully about before sharing with children. That being said, some parents/teachers may find it a valuable tool when dealing with loss and inquisitive little minds.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1935429374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1935429374" />
    <a title="Lily Moore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64574538-lily-moore"><img alt="Lily Moore" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1935429374?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily Moore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily Moore" href="/user/show/64574538-lily-moore">Lily Moore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64574538-lily-moore?shelf=betterment-list">betterment-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935429374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9840515397553275143">Duck, Death and Tulip by Wolf Erlbruch is a book about death and how the duck discovers it but death is not a scary thing but a friend. This picture book is in the 1st person being told by duck and death. This makes it an explicit message as from the title you can tell that the story is going to be about death. <br/><br/>Throughout the book the duck is always on the left of the page while death is always on the right unless they go to the pond, duck realises she is not dead yet, climb the tree and finally</span>
  <span id="freeText9840515397553275143" style="display:none">Duck, Death and Tulip by Wolf Erlbruch is a book about death and how the duck discovers it but death is not a scary thing but a friend. This picture book is in the 1st person being told by duck and death. This makes it an explicit message as from the title you can tell that the story is going to be about death. <br /><br />Throughout the book the duck is always on the left of the page while death is always on the right unless they go to the pond, duck realises she is not dead yet, climb the tree and finally when she dies. This is when she is being carried into the lake and this means that duck is more secure until they go on an adventure which is a risk putting him on the right. This book doesn't have a background only shows you what is in the foreground but most importantly only what you need to see. I think is has been done to show a powerful message and to only concentrate on what is important to get the message across. Also throughout the book, you are always at the characters level which indicates you are going on the adventure with them. The framing in the book covers the whole page which means you are part of the story and seeing death and the duck as your friends.<br />The colours are dull which means a quieter meaning you will have inside as its a sensitive subject. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book and found it interesting that a picture book with a deep meaning can be aimed at children to be able to understand death is a friendly way, meaning that children shouldn't be scared of death. I did find the book to move me as you can relate to it if you have lost a loved one in a weird calming way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9840515397553275143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2183033703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2183033703" />
    <a title="Emma Hamilton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65993238-emma-hamilton"><img alt="Emma Hamilton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507582140p2/65993238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2183033703?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Hamilton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Hamilton" href="/user/show/65993238-emma-hamilton">Emma Hamilton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65993238-emma-hamilton?shelf=ks2">ks2</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183033703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12672629888998283570">This book shows a duck who is being followed by a character named death- the duck befriends death and they begin to do things together like swimming and climbing trees. Eventually the duck becomes cold and stops breathing. Death places the duck on the river with a tulip. The book ends with death saying he felt a little moved by the whole thing but then he says 'that's life'.<br/><br/>Interesting book about the idea that death follows you throughout life. The ending which says 'thats life' makes you think </span>
  <span id="freeText12672629888998283570" style="display:none">This book shows a duck who is being followed by a character named death- the duck befriends death and they begin to do things together like swimming and climbing trees. Eventually the duck becomes cold and stops breathing. Death places the duck on the river with a tulip. The book ends with death saying he felt a little moved by the whole thing but then he says 'that's life'.<br /><br />Interesting book about the idea that death follows you throughout life. The ending which says 'thats life' makes you think about the process of life and death and for children this could be quite an abrupt way of looking at things. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12672629888998283570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vTMGm2XNH9VTZuD6XWLDX7gHzpfcVduAFz2fxjA9Z4ipF+p7FjHzbDKUIuhkTi+jmYSY0vVQaKXl/jLtX8UQiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LvHeeNHiCoZVNdCJjoexqB6AdkzzGQizW3eP7E/vgKU61TKYoh7mPzTHEpu3q11UPwMgCdocu5aptCLHIBf3pg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/114750.Wolf_Erlbruch">About Wolf Erlbruch</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/114750.Wolf_Erlbruch"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1285085211p3/114750.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/114750.Wolf_Erlbruch">Wolf Erlbruch
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
66
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17089154929730624808">Wolf Erlbruch (born 1949 in Wuppertal, Germany) is an award-winning illustrator and writer of children's books. He combines various techniques for the artwork in his books, including cutting and pasting, drawing, and painting. His style is sometimes surrealist and is widely copied inside and outside Germany, and some of his story books discuss adult topics such as death and the meaning of life. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText17089154929730624808" style="display:none">Wolf Erlbruch (born 1949 in Wuppertal, Germany) is an award-winning illustrator and writer of children's books. He combines various techniques for the artwork in his books, including cutting and pasting, drawing, and painting. His style is sometimes surrealist and is widely copied inside and outside Germany, and some of his story books discuss adult topics such as death and the meaning of life. They have won many awards, including the Deutscher Jugendliteraturpreis in 1993 and 2003, and the Hans Christian Andersen Award for illustration in 2006.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17089154929730624808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
